# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

### **Core GroupCoordinator Components (41 Java files)**

1. **GroupCoordinator Interface & Service:**
   - `GroupCoordinator.java` - Main interface
   - `GroupCoordinatorService.java` - Primary implementation
   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.java` - Shard-level coordinator

2. **State Machine Implementation:**
   - `ClassicGroupState.java` - Enum defining the 5 states:
     - **Empty** - Initial state
     - **PreparingRebalance** - Transition state for rebalancing
     - **CompletingRebalance** - After join completion
     - **Stable** - Normal operation
     - **Dead** - Terminal state

3. **Request Handlers (JoinGroup/SyncGroup):**
   - Located in `GroupCoordinatorService`, `GroupCoordinatorShard`, and `GroupMetadataManager`
   - Methods: `joinGroup()`, `syncGroup()`, `handleJoinGroupRequest()`, `handleSyncGroupRequest()`
   - Support for classic and modern group types

4. **Heartbeat Expiry Detection:**
   - `rescheduleClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` - Schedules member heartbeat timeouts
   - `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` - Handles expired heartbeats
   - Three heartbeat handlers: `consumerGroupHeartbeat()`, `shareGroupHeartbeat()`, `streamsGroupHeartbeat()`

5. **Group Implementations:**
   - **Classic Groups**: `ClassicGroup.java`, `ClassicGroupMember.java`
   - **Consumer Groups**: `ConsumerGroup.java`, `ConsumerGroupMember.java`
   - **Share Groups**: `ShareGroup.java`, `ShareGroupMember.java`
   - **Streams Groups**: `StreamsGroup.java`, `StreamsGroupMember.java`

SyncGroup)\\n\\nJoinGroup and SyncGroup request handling is implemented through:\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService**: Contains `joinGroup()` and `syncGroup()` methods that delegate to `GroupCoordinatorShard`\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard**: Contains `handleJoinGroupRequest()` and `handleSyncGroupRequest()` methods that forward to `GroupMetadataManager`\\n- **GroupMetadataManager**: Contains the actual implementation logic including `classicGroupJoinToClassicGroup()`, `classicGroupSyncToClassicGroup()`, and modern group variants\\n\\n## Group Metadata State Machine\\n\\nThe state machine is implemented through the `ClassicGroupState` enum in `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java`, which defines the five states:\\n- **Empty**: Initial state when a group is created\\n- **PreparingRebalance**: Transition state when a rebalance is triggered\\n- **CompletingRebalance**: State after all members have joined\\n- **Stable**: Normal operation state\\n- **Dead**: Terminal state when a group is removed\\n\\nState transitions are controlled in `ClassicGroup.java` and validated through the `transitionTo()` method.\\n\\n## Group Implementations\\n\\nDifferent group types are implemented as classes extending from `Group` interface or `ModernGroup` base class:\\n\\n1. **Classic Groups** (`ClassicGroup.java`, `ClassicGroupMember.java`): Legacy consumer groups using the Classic protocol\\n2. **Consumer Groups** (`ConsumerGroup.java`, `ConsumerGroupMember.java`): Modern consumer groups with the newer consumer protocol\\n3. **Share Groups** (`ShareGroup.java`, `ShareGroupMember.java`): Groups for share consumption patterns\\n4. **Streams Groups** (`StreamsGroup.java`, `StreamsGroupMember.java`): Groups for Kafka Streams applications\\n\\n## Heartbeat Expiry Detection\\n\\nHeartbeat management and expiry detection is implemented through:\\n- **Scheduling**: `rescheduleClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` in `GroupMetadataManager` schedules heartbeat timeouts for members\\n- **Expiry Detection**: `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` handles expiration when heartbeats timeout\\n- **Heartbeat Handlers**: \\n  - `consumerGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles consumer group heartbeats\\n  - `shareGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles share group heartbeats\\n  - `streamsGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles streams group heartbeats\\n\\nThese heartbeat methods are coordinated across `GroupCoordinatorService`, `GroupCoordinatorShard`, and `GroupMetadataManager`.\\n\\n## Assignment Management\\n\\nPartition assignment to group members is handled through multiple builder classes:\\n- `UniformAssignor`, `RangeAssignor`, `SimpleAssignor`: Partition assignment strategies\\n- `CurrentAssignmentBuilder`: Builds current member assignments\\n- `TargetAssignmentBuilder`: Computes target assignments for rebalancing\\n- Various assignment builders for different group types (consumer, share, streams)\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n\\n- **GroupCoordinatorConfig**: Configuration management for group coordinator settings\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager**: Manages committed offsets for groups\\n- **GroupCoordinatorMetrics**: Tracks metrics for group coordinator operations\\n- **GroupCoordinatorRecordSerde**: Serialization/deserialization of group metadata records\\n\\nThe entire system works together to provide a robust group coordination protocol that handles member discovery, assignment, rebalancing, and failure detection across different consumer group types in Kafka.\"\n}\n",

GroupCoordinator is implemented as an interface in `GroupCoordinator.java` that defines the main API for group coordination. This interface is implemented by `GroupCoordinatorService.java`, which acts as the main service handler for all group-related requests.\\n\\n## Request Handlers (JoinGroup and SyncGroup)\\n\\nJoinGroup and SyncGroup request handling is implemented through:\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService**: Contains `joinGroup()` and `syncGroup()` methods that delegate to `GroupCoordinatorShard`\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard**: Contains `handleJoinGroupRequest()` and `handleSyncGroupRequest()` methods that forward to `GroupMetadataManager`\\n- **GroupMetadataManager**: Contains the actual implementation logic including `classicGroupJoinToClassicGroup()`, `classicGroupSyncToClassicGroup()`, and modern group variants\\n\\n## Group Metadata State Machine\\n\\nThe state machine is implemented through the `ClassicGroupState` enum in `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java`, which defines the five states:\\n- **Empty**: Initial state when a group is created\\n- **PreparingRebalance**: Transition state when a rebalance is triggered\\n- **CompletingRebalance**: State after all members have joined\\n- **Stable**: Normal operation state\\n- **Dead**: Terminal state when a group is removed\\n\\nState transitions are controlled in `ClassicGroup.java` and validated through the `transitionTo()` method.\\n\\n## Group Implementations\\n\\nDifferent group types are implemented as classes extending from `Group` interface or `ModernGroup` base class:\\n\\n1. **Classic Groups** (`ClassicGroup.java`, `ClassicGroupMember.java`): Legacy consumer groups using the Classic protocol\\n2. **Consumer Groups** (`ConsumerGroup.java`, `ConsumerGroupMember.java`): Modern consumer groups with the newer consumer protocol\\n3. **Share Groups** (`ShareGroup.java`, `ShareGroupMember.java`): Groups for share consumption patterns\\n4. **Streams Groups** (`StreamsGroup.java`, `StreamsGroupMember.java`): Groups for Kafka Streams applications\\n\\n## Heartbeat Expiry Detection\\n\\nHeartbeat management and expiry detection is implemented through:\\n- **Scheduling**: `rescheduleClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` in `GroupMetadataManager` schedules heartbeat timeouts for members\\n- **Expiry Detection**: `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` handles expiration when heartbeats timeout\\n- **Heartbeat Handlers**: \\n  - `consumerGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles consumer group heartbeats\\n  - `shareGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles share group heartbeats\\n  - `streamsGroupHeartbeat()`: Handles streams group heartbeats\\n\\nThese heartbeat methods are coordinated across `GroupCoordinatorService`, `GroupCoordinatorShard`, and `GroupMetadataManager`.\\n\\n## Assignment Management\\n\\nPartition assignment to group members is handled through multiple builder classes:\\n- `UniformAssignor`, `RangeAssignor`, `SimpleAssignor`: Partition assignment strategies\\n- `CurrentAssignmentBuilder`: Builds current member assignments\\n- `TargetAssignmentBuilder`: Computes target assignments for rebalancing\\n- Various assignment builders for different group types (consumer, share, streams)\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n\\n- **GroupCoordinatorConfig**: Configuration management for group coordinator settings\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager**: Manages committed offsets for groups\\n- **GroupCoordinatorMetrics**: Tracks metrics for group coordinator operations\\n- **GroupCoordinatorRecordSerde**: Serialization/deserialization of group metadata records\\n\\nThe entire system works together to provide a robust group coordination protocol that handles member discovery, assignment, rebalancing, and failure detection across different consumer
